The Ruling on Self-Admiration and Its Effect on Deeds
Author explains ruling on ‘ujb and refutes an opposing view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling on ‘ujb (self-admiration) and why only riyā’ and ‘ujb nullify reward, while other sins do not, according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
Only riyā’ and ‘ujb nullify reward; other sins are erased by good deeds.

Self-admiration (‘ujb) is a spiritual disease that can nullify the reward of the deed it accompanies. In this passage, the author clarifies the ruling based on Imam Abu Hanifa’s position, provides scriptural evidence, and refutes the view that all bad traits nullify rewards. You will see how the author handles conflicting hadiths to preserve the core principle of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic text and its English translation. Notice the structure: the author states the ruling, gives evidence, presents an opposing view, and then rebuts it point by point.
Pay attention to the two hadiths used by the opposing commentator.
2
Identify the main ruling and its basis
The passage starts by stating that ‘ujb nullifies reward. It then notes that Imam Abu Hanifa only mentioned riyā’ and ‘ujb, implying other sins don’t nullify. Find the Quranic verse and sacred hadith that support this.
The verse (Hūd 11:114) and the hadith qudsi are key.
3
Examine the opposing view and its evidence
A commentator argues that other bad traits also nullify reward, citing a hadith about five things that break the fast. Note how the author interprets this hadith to mean breaking the perfection, not the validity of the fast.
The author also refutes a second hadith about bad character spoiling deeds.
4
Understand the author’s rebuttals
The author provides two rebuttals: first, the ‘five breakers’ hadith is about perfection; second, the ‘bad character’ hadith refers specifically to riyā’ and ‘ujb. See how he reconciles these with the primary evidence.
This shows the methodology of Ahl al-Sunnah in harmonizing texts.
5
Reflect on the broader principle
Consider why only these two sins nullify reward. The passage implies that other sins are minor or are erased by good deeds, as per the Quranic promise. This preserves hope in Allah’s mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا العجب) أي وكذا حكم العجب في أنه يبطل أجر العمل الذي وقع فيه العجب، وفي اقتصار حكم الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله على الرياء والعجب دون سائر الآثام إشعار بأن باقي السيئات لا تبطل الحسنات، بل قال الله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ الْحَسَنتِ يُذْهِبْنَ السَّيَاتِ﴾ [هود: ١١٤]، وذلك للحديث القدسي: ((سبقت رحمتي غضبي)). وقد خالفه شارح حيث قال: وكذا غيرهما من الأخلاق السيئة يبطل أجور الأعمال الحسنة، واستدل بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: خمس يفطرن الصائم: الغيبة والكذب، والنميمة، واليمين الكاذبة والنظر بشهوة. ولم يعرف تأويل الحديث بأن المراد به أنه يفطر كمال الصوم ويبطل جماله لا أصله، فإن النظر بشهوة صغيرة، وهو لا يبطل العمل، لا عند أهل السنة ولا عند المعتزلة. وأما استدلاله بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: ((سوء الخلق يفسد العمل كما يفسد الخل العسل)) فمدفوع؛ لأن الحديث مؤوّل بأن سوء خلقه من ريائه وعجبه يفسد ثواب عمله، جمعا بين الأدلة كما بينه هو مقتضى مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة.
And likewise self-admiration (al-‘ujb), i.e., the ruling of self-admiration is likewise in that it nullifies the reward of the deed in which self-admiration occurred. And in the limitation of the ruling of Imam al-A‘zam (may Allah have mercy on him) to riyā’ (show-off) and ‘ujb excluding other sins is an indication that the remaining evil deeds do not nullify good deeds. Rather, Allah the Exalted said: {Indeed, good deeds remove evil deeds} [Hūd 11:114], and that is due to the sacred hadith: 'My mercy prevailed over My wrath.' And a commentator (shāriḥ) opposed him and said: Likewise, other bad character traits nullify the rewards of good deeds, and he adduced the Prophet’s ﷺ saying: 'Five things break the fast of the fasting person: backbiting, lying, slander, false oath, and looking with desire.' And he did not realize the interpretation of the hadith that what is meant is that it breaks the perfection of the fast and nullifies its beauty, not its essence. For looking with desire is a minor sin, and it does not nullify the deed, neither according to Ahl al-Sunnah nor according to the Mu‘tazila. As for his adducing the Prophet’s ﷺ saying: 'Bad character spoils the deed just as vinegar spoils honey,' it is rebutted because the hadith is interpreted to mean that his bad character from his riyā’ and ‘ujb spoils the reward of his deed, reconciling the evidences as he explained it is the requirement of the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jamā‘ah.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal ruling on self-admiration (‘ujb). It begins by stating that ‘ujb nullifies the reward of the deed in which it occurs, and notes that Imam Abu Hanifa (Imam al-A‘zam) only mentioned riyā’ and ‘ujb as nullifiers, implying that other sins do not nullify good deeds. This is supported by the Quranic verse (Hūd 11:114) and a sacred hadith. The author then presents an opposing view from a commentator who extends nullification to other bad traits, citing a hadith about five things that break the fast. The author refutes this by interpreting the hadith as affecting the perfection of the fast, not its validity, and noting that looking with desire is a minor sin. He further refutes a second hadith about bad character spoiling deeds by specifying that it refers to riyā’ and ‘ujb. The passage concludes that the correct position is that of Ahl al-Sunnah.

The Priority of Steadfastness Over Wonders
Quotes Abu Ali al-Juzjani and al-Suhrawardi on seeking istiqama.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why spiritual steadfastness (istiqama) is more important than seeking miraculous wonders (karamat), and the wisdom behind why Allah grants wonders to some.

Core Idea
Steadfastness in obedience is the true wonder, not supernatural events.

This lesson presents a profound spiritual principle from two great scholars: Abu Ali al-Juzjani and Shihab al-Din al-Suhrawardi. They caution against longing for extraordinary experiences and instead direct the seeker to focus on steadfastness in worship. The passage explains that the soul's desire for wonders can lead to self-doubt, while true faith finds its strength in consistent obedience to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the direct, personal advice from al-Juzjani and the more detailed explanation from al-Suhrawardi.
The passage uses key terms like 'istiqama' and 'karama'—important to understand.
2
Identify the two quotes
Distinguish between al-Juzjani's concise statement and al-Suhrawardi's expansion. Understand how al-Suhrawardi builds on the earlier advice.
3
Reflect on al-Suhrawardi's wisdom
Consider why Allah grants wonders to some sincere strivers: to increase their certainty and strengthen their resolve in renouncing the world and controlling desires. Reflect on how this contrasts with the seeker's own desire for wonders.
Al-Suhrawardi explains that if one understood this secret, the matter would be easy.
4
Apply the lesson
Think about your own spiritual practice. Are you ever discouraged by not experiencing extraordinary events? How can focusing on istiqama transform your approach to worship and self-discipline?
The key takeaway is that istiqama itself is the complete wonder.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو علي الجوزجاني رحمه الله: كن طالبا للاستقامة لا طالبا للكرامة، فإن نفسك كة في طلب الكرامة، وربك يطلب منك الاستقامة». قال الشيخ السهروردي رحمه الله في عوارفه: «وهذا أصل كبير في الباب، فإنّ كثيراً من المجتهدين المتعبدين سمعوا سلف الصالحين المتقدمين وما منحوا من الكرامات وخوارق العادات، فنفوسهم لا تزال تَتَطَلَّع إلى شيء من ويحبون أن يرزقوا شيئا منه، ولعل أحدهم يبقى منكسر القلب متهما لنفسه في صحة عمله حيث لم يحصل له خارق، ولو علموا سر ذلك لهان عليهم الأمر، فيعلم أن الله يفتح على بعض المجاهدين الصادقين من ذلك ،بابا والحكمة فيه أن يزداد مما يرى من خوارق العادات وآثار القدرة يقينا فيقوى عزمه على الزهد في الدنيا والخروج من دواعي الهوى، فسبيل الصادق مطالبة النفس بالاستقامة فهى كل الكرامة، انتهى.
Abu Ali al-Juzjani said: 'Be a seeker of steadfastness (istiqama), not a seeker of wonders, for your soul is eager in seeking wonders, and your Lord asks you for steadfastness.' Al-Shaykh al-Suhrawardi said in his 'Awarif: 'This is a great principle in this matter. Many striving worshippers heard about the early righteous predecessors and what they were granted of wonders and extraordinary events, and their souls still aspire to something of that, and they love to be given something of it. Perhaps one of them remains broken-hearted, accusing himself of the validity of his actions because he has not obtained an extraordinary event. If they knew the secret of that, the matter would be easy for them. They would know that Allah opens for some of the sincere strivers a door to that, and the wisdom in it is that by seeing extraordinary events and signs of power, one increases in certainty, so his resolve strengthens in renouncing the world and departing from the motives of desire. So the way of the sincere is to demand of oneself steadfastness, for it is the whole wonder.'
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage presents spiritual advice from two prominent Sufi scholars. Abu Ali al-Juzjani advises to seek istiqama (steadfastness in obedience) rather than karamat (extraordinary wonders), because the soul naturally craves wonders while Allah requires steadfastness. Al-Suhrawardi expands on this: many devoted worshippers who hear about the wonders granted to the early righteous become desirous of such experiences, and if they do not obtain them, they may become disheartened and doubt their own sincerity. He explains that Allah grants wonders only to some sincere strivers as a means to increase their certainty and strengthen their resolve in renouncing the world and controlling desires. The true path for the sincere is to focus on istiqama, which is the greatest wonder of all. This lesson serves as a caution against seeking supernatural experiences for their own sake.

الجوزجاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: That miraculous wonders (karamat) are the goal of spiritual striving and their absence indicates failure.
Correction: The text teaches that steadfastness in worship (istiqama) is the true wonder, and that wonders are only granted to some for specific wisdom, not as a measure of one's spiritual state.

The Superiority of Religious Knowledge Over Worldly Knowledge
Concludes that religious knowledge is superior and quotes hadith on firasa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why religious knowledge is superior to worldly knowledge and how the believer's intuition (firasa) is a gift from Allah.

Core Idea
Religious knowledge protects your faith; worldly knowledge can distract.

This concluding passage from the Manah al-Rawdh al-Azhar sums up the comparison between religious and worldly knowledge. The author makes a clear value judgment: religious knowledge is more important because lacking it harms one's faith. He then reinforces this with a prophetic hadith about the believer's intuition, which sees by Allah's light.

3
Reflect on the hadith

والحاصل أن كشف العلم بالأمور الشرعية خير من كشف العلم بالأمور الكونية مع أن عدم الأول ونقصانه مضرة في الدين بخلاف عدم الثاني بل وربما يكون عدمه أنفع له، ثم اعلم أنه قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «اتقوا فراسة المؤمن فإنه ينظر بنور الله» ثم قرأ قوله تعالى:

Commentary
This final passage sums up the relative value of different kinds of knowledge. The author asserts that unveiling (kashf) of religious knowledge (al-'ilm bi'l-umur al-shar'iyya) is superior to unveiling of natural/cosmic knowledge (al-'ilm bi'l-umur al-kawniyya). The reason is that lacking or having deficient religious knowledge harms one's religion, whereas lacking cosmic knowledge is not harmful; indeed, sometimes it is even beneficial because it prevents distraction from spiritual goals. Then the author quotes a well-known hadith about the believer's intuition (firasa), which sees by Allah's light. The text ends with the beginning of a Quranic verse that the Prophet recited after the hadith, but the verse is not provided. This passage reinforces the idea that the real treasure is spiritual insight and religious knowledge, not supernatural displays.

Definition of Iman: Confession and Affirmation
Definition of iman as iqrar and tasdiq, with proofs from Qur'an.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of iman according to Abu Hanifa, which requires both verbal confession and heartfelt affirmation, and why neither alone is sufficient.

Core Idea
Iman is not just words or knowledge—it is both spoken and believed.

The author defines iman as a composite of two elements: verbal confession (iqrar) and heartfelt affirmation (tasdiq). This lesson unpacks that definition, drawing on Imam Abu Hanifa's own words from his book al-Wasiyya. You will see why neither element alone qualifies as faith, and how the Qur'an supports this position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the key terms: iqrar, tasdiq, ma'rifa.
The author gives a definition and then two clear proofs.
2
Identify the two components
Find where the author states that iman is iqrar and tasdiq. Note the order: iqrar is mentioned first because it is outward, even though tasdiq is the inner foundation.
3
Understand the two proofs
The author uses two Qur'anic proofs: one against iqrar alone (hypocrites) and one against tasdiq alone (People of the Book). Ask yourself: why does each group fall short?
This shows that iman requires both tongue and heart.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإيمان هو الإقرار أي بلسانه بالتحقيق والتصديق أي بالجنان وفق التوفيق، وتقديم الإقرار للإشعار بأنه الأول في مقام الإظهار وإن كان الثاني هو المبدوء به في حال الاعتبار، ولأن الشارع اكتفى بمجرد الإقرار ولم يفرّق في الحكم بين المرافق والمنافق وبين الأبرار والفجار. وقال الإمام الأعظم في كتابه "الوصية": الإيمان إقرار باللسان وتصديق بالجنان، والإقرار وحده لا يكون إيمانا؛ لأنه لو كان إيمانا لكان المنافقون كلهم مؤمنين، وكذلك المعرفة وحدها أي مجرد التصديق لا يكون إيمانا ؛ لأنها لو كانت إيمانا لكان أهل الكتاب كلهم مؤمنين، قال الله تعالى في حق المنافقين : وَاللهُ يَشْهَدُ إِنَّ الْمُنْفِقِينَ لَكَذِبُونَ ﴾ [المنافقون: ١]، أي في دعواهم الإيمان حيث لا تصديق لهم، وقال الله تعالى في حق أهل الكتاب : الَّذِينَ اتَيْتُهُمُ الْكِتَبَ يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ ابْنَا وَهُمْ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٤٦) انتهى.
And iman is al-iqrar (confession), i.e., with the tongue in verification, and al-tasdiq (affirmation), i.e., with the heart according to divine facilitation. And the precedence of iqrar is to indicate that it is the first in the position of manifestation, even though the second is what is begun with in the state of consideration, and because the Lawgiver is content with mere iqrar and did not differentiate in the ruling between the hypocrite and the sincere, nor between the righteous and the wicked. And Imam al-A'zam said in his book 'al-Wasiyya': Iman is iqrar with the tongue and tasdiq with the heart. Iqrar alone is not iman, because if it were iman, then all hypocrites would be believers. Likewise, ma'rifa (knowledge) alone, i.e., mere tasdiq, is not iman, because if it were iman, then all the People of the Book would be believers. Allah Almighty said concerning the hypocrites: 'Allah bears witness that the hypocrites are liars' (al-Munafiqun 1), i.e., in their claim of iman where they have no tasdiq. And Allah Almighty said concerning the People of the Book: 'Those to whom We gave the Book recognize him as they recognize their sons' (al-Baqarah 146). End.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a definition of iman (faith). The author first defines iman as iqrar (verbal confession) and tasdiq (heartsfelt affirmation). He notes that iqrar is mentioned first because it is the outward manifestation, even though tasdiq is the inner foundation that logically comes first. Then he explains why the Lawgiver accepts mere verbal confession in this world: to avoid making a distinction between hypocrites and true believers in worldly rulings—both are treated as Muslims outwardly. However, he then quotes Imam Abu Hanifa from his book 'al-Wasiyya' to clarify the true nature of iman: it requires both tongue and heart. Iqrar alone is insufficient, because if it were enough, hypocrites would be believers, but Allah calls them liars in Surah al-Munafiqun since their confession lacks tasdiq. Similarly, tasdiq (or ma'rifa) alone is insufficient, because if it were enough, the People of the Book would be believers since they recognize the truth of the Prophet, yet Allah condemns them as disbelievers. Thus iman is a composite of both verbal confession and heartfelt affirmation.

Key Terms
الإيمان (al-iman)
الإقرار (al-iqrar)
التصديق (al-tasdiq)
المعرفة (al-ma'rifa)
المنافقون (al-munafiqun)
أهل الكتاب (ahl al-kitab)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some equate iman with mere verbal confession alone (like the Murji'a) or mere knowledge alone (like some rationalists).
Correction: The passage clarifies that both iqrar and tasdiq are necessary; neither alone suffices, as proven by the Qur'anic examples of hypocrites and People of the Book.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that mere iqrar (verbal confession) is not sufficient for iman?
A) Because the tongue can speak falsely
B) Because hypocrites make such a confession yet are disbelievers
C) Because Allah commands silence
D) Because iman requires action

Key Takeaway
Iman is the combination of verbal confession and heartfelt affirmation; neither alone is sufficient, as shown by the hypocrites and the People of the Book.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the shahada, do your words ever feel hollow? This lesson warns that hypocrisy is just that—words without inner truth. Commit today to examine your heart before you speak: ask Allah to make your confession sincere.
?
The People of the Book recognized the Prophet but rejected him. Is there any truth in Islam that you 'know' is right yet fail to live by—in your charity, prayer, or honesty? What step will you take today to move from mere knowledge to active faith?
?
If you were to stand before Allah tonight, would your outward confession match your inner conviction? The lesson demands both. Write down one area where you need to strengthen your inner tasdiq and one area where your outer iqrar needs improvement. Then act on it.

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
5 min
The Definition of Iman as Iqrar and Tasdiq
Sanusi defines iman and explains the precedence of iqrar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classical definition of iman as both verbal acknowledgement (iqrar) and inner conviction (tasdiq) and why iqrar is mentioned first.

Core Idea
Faith is spoken acknowledgement and heartfelt conviction together.

Sanusi opens by defining iman in its two essential components: iqrar (verbal declaration) and tasdiq (inner conviction). He explains why the Lawgiver presents iqrar first in outward rulings, even though inward conviction is the foundation. This lesson lays the groundwork for understanding the relationship between belief and its expression.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the phrasing: 'al-iqrar ... bi lisanihi' and 'al-tasdiq ... bi al-janan'.
Imam al-A'zam later repeats this definition in his work 'Al-Wasiyya'.
2
Understand why iqrar is mentioned first
Sanusi gives two reasons: (1) iqrar is the first manifestation outwardly, even though tasdiq comes first in consideration; (2) the Lawgiver accepts mere iqrar for worldly rulings, not distinguishing between believer and hypocrite.
This highlights that iqrar is the basis for legal rulings, while tasdiq is the basis for true faith.
3
Reflect on the wisdom behind the order
Ask yourself: Why would Allah accept a mere verbal declaration in worldly matters? The answer points to the practicality of Islamic law – it judges by the apparent, while the inner reality is left to Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإيمان هو الإقرار أي بلسانه بالتحقيق والتصديق أي بالجنان وفق التوفيق، وتقديم الإقرار للإشعار بأنه الأول في مقام الإظهار وإن كان الثاني هو المبدوء به في حال الاعتبار، ولأن الشارع اكتفى بمجرد الإقرار ولم يفرّق في الحكم بين المرافق والمنافق وبين الأبرار والفجار. وقال الإمام الأعظم في كتابه "الوصية": الإيمان إقرار باللسان وتصديق بالجنان، والإقرار وحده لا يكون إيمانا؛ لأنه لو كان إيمانا لكان المنافقون كلهم مؤمنين، وكذلك المعرفة وحدها أي مجرد التصديق لا يكون إيمانا؛ لأنها لو كانت إيمانا لكان أهل الكتاب كلهم مؤمنين، قال الله تعالى في حق المنافقين: وَاللهُ يَشْهَدُ إِنَّ الْمُنَافِقِينَ لَكَاذِبُونَ [المنافقون: ١]، أي في دعواهم الإيمان حيث لا تصديق لهم، وقال الله تعالى في حق أهل الكتاب: الَّذِينَ آتَيْنَاهُمُ الْكِتَابَ يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَهُمْ [البقرة: ١٤٦] انتهى. والمقصود أن مجرد معرفة أهل الكتاب بالله ورسوله لا ينفعهم حيث ما أقرّوا بنبوة محمد صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ورسالته إليهم وإلى الخلق كافة، فانهم كانوا يزعمون أنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم مبعوث إلى العرب خاصة، فإقرارهم بهذا الطريق لا يكون خالصاً. ثم التصديق ركن حسن لعينه لا يحتمل السقوط في حال من الأحوال بخلاف الإقرار، فإنه شرط أو شطر وركن حسن لغيره، ولهذا يسقط في حال الإكراه وحصول الأعذار. وهذا لأن اللسان ترجمان الجنان فيكون دليل التصديق وجوداً وعدماً، فإذا بدّله بغيره في وقت يكون متمكناً من إظهاره كان كافراً، وأما إذا زال تمكنه من الإظهار بالإكراه لم يصر كافراً؛ لأن سبب الخوف على نفسه دليل ظاهر على بقاء التصديق في قلبه وأن الحامل له على هذا التبديل حاجته إلى دفع المهلكة عن نفسه، لا تبديل الاعتقاد في حقه كما أشار إليه قوله تعالى: مَنْ كَفَرَ بِاللَّهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ إِيمَانِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنٌّ بِالْإِيمَانِ وَلَكِنْ مَنْ شَرَحَ بِالْكُفْرِ صَدْرًا فَعَلَيْهِمْ غَضَبٌ مِنَ اللَّهِ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ عَظِيمٌ [النحل: ١٠٦]، فأما تبديله في وقت تمكنه دليل على تبديل اعتقاده، فكان ركن الإيمان وجوداً وعدماً كما صرح به شمس الأئمة السرخسي، إلا أن صاحب "العُدة" وهو أبو البركات عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمود النسفي رحمه الله صرح بأن الإقرار شرط إجراء الأحكام وهو مختار الأشاعرة، وعليه أبو منصور الماتريدي، ثم في حذف المؤمن به في كلام الإمام الأعظم إشعار بأن الإيمان الإجمالي كاف في مقام المرام. فالتحقيق أن الإيمان هو تصديق النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم بالقلب في جميع ما علم بالضرورة مجيئه به من عند الله إجمالاً وأنه كاف في الخروج عن عهدة الإيمان ولا تنحط درجته عن الإيمان التفصيلي، كذا في "شرح العقائد"، إلا أن الأولى أن يقال: إجمالاً إن لوحظ
And faith (al-iman) is acknowledgement (al-iqrar) i.e. with the tongue, by verification, and inner conviction (al-tasdiq) i.e. with the heart, according to divine success. And the precedence of acknowledgement is to indicate that it is first in the position of manifestation, although inner conviction is the one that is started with in the case of consideration, and because the Lawgiver sufficed with mere acknowledgement and did not differentiate in the ruling between the pious and the hypocrite, nor between the righteous and the wicked. And Imam al-A'zam said in his book "Al-Wasiyya": Faith is acknowledgement with the tongue and inner conviction with the heart. Acknowledgement alone does not constitute faith; because if it were faith, all the hypocrites would be believers. Likewise, knowledge (al-ma'rifa) alone i.e. mere inner conviction does not constitute faith; because if it were faith, all the People of the Book would be believers. Allah Almighty said concerning the hypocrites: "And Allah bears witness that the hypocrites are certainly liars" [Qur'an 63:1], i.e. in their claim of faith while they have no inner conviction. And Allah Almighty said concerning the People of the Book: "Those whom We gave the Book recognize him as they recognize their own sons" [Qur'an 2:146]. End. And the meaning is that mere knowledge of the People of the Book about Allah and His Messenger does not benefit them since they did not acknowledge the prophethood of Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) and his message to them and to all creation, for they claimed that he (peace and blessings be upon him) was sent only to the Arabs specifically, so their acknowledgement in this way is not pure. Then inner conviction is an essential pillar in itself (rukn hasan li'aynihi) that cannot possibly fall away in any circumstance, unlike acknowledgement, for it is a condition (shart) or part (shatr) and a pillar for something else (rukn hasan li-ghayrihi). For this reason it falls away in the case of coercion and when excuses occur. This is because the tongue is the interpreter of the heart, so it is an indicator of inner conviction both in existence and absence. If one substitutes it with something else at a time when one is able to express it, he becomes a disbeliever. But if his ability to express it ceases due to coercion, he does not become a disbeliever, because the cause of fear for his life is an apparent indication of the persistence of inner conviction in his heart and that what drives him to this substitution is his need to repel harm from himself, not a change of belief in his case, as indicated by the saying of Allah Almighty: "Whoever disbelieves in Allah after his belief – except for one who is coerced while his heart is at rest with faith – but whoever opens their breast to disbelief, upon them is wrath from Allah and for them is a great punishment" [Qur'an 16:106]. As for his substituting it at a time when he is able, it is an indication of his belief change, so it becomes the pillar of faith both in existence and non-existence, as Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi stated. However, the author of "Al-'Umdah" – and he is Abu al-Barakat Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Mahmud al-Nasafi (may Allah have mercy on him) – stated that acknowledgement is a condition for the application of rulings, which is the choice of the Ash'aris, and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi also held this. Then, in the omission of the object of belief in the words of Imam al-A'zam, there is an indication that summary faith (al-iman al-ijmali) is sufficient in the intended purpose. The verification is that faith is inner conviction in the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) with the heart in all that is known by necessity to have come from him from Allah, summarily, and that it is sufficient to discharge the obligation of faith, and its rank is not lower than detailed faith (al-iman al-tafsili). Thus in "Sharh al-'Aqa'id", except that the better thing to say is: summarily if it is considered.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage defines faith (iman) and explains the roles of its two components: iqrar (verbal declaration) and tasdiq (inner conviction). The author begins by stating that iqrar is with the tongue and tasdiq with the heart, noting that iqrar is mentioned first to show it is the initial outward manifestation, though tasdiq is the starting point in consideration. The Lawgiver (the Prophet) accepted mere iqrar in rulings, not distinguishing between the pious and the hypocrite in outward judgment. The author then quotes Imam al-A'zam from his work 'Al-Wasiyya': iman is both iqrar and tasdiq; neither alone suffices. He supports this with Quranic evidence: the hypocrites are liars because they lack tasdiq, and the People of the Book know the truth but lack proper iqrar (they did not acknowledge Muhammad's prophet hood universally). The author then explains that tasdiq is an essential pillar that never falls away, while iqrar is a conditional pillar that drops under coercion. He elaborates: the tongue indicates what is in the heart; if one is able to express it but substitutes it, he becomes a disbeliever; if coerced, the fear shows tasdiq remains. He cites Quran 16:106. He then mentions scholarly views: Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi considered iqrar as an integral part of faith, while Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi and the Ash'aris considered it a condition for worldly rulings. He concludes that summary faith (tasdiq in all that the Prophet brought, without details) is sufficient and not inferior to detailed faith.

Key Terms
الإيمان (al-iman)
الإقرار (al-iqrar)
التصديق (al-tasdiq)
المنافقون (al-munafiqun)
الأبرار (al-abrar)
الفجار (al-fujjar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is iqrar (verbal declaration) mentioned first in the definition of iman?
A) Because it is more important than tasdiq
B) Because it is the first thing that appears outwardly and the Lawgiver accepts it for worldly rulings
C) Because tasdiq cannot exist without iqrar
D) Because it is the only component accepted by Allah

Key Takeaway
Iman is defined as both verbal acknowledgement (iqrar) and inner conviction (tasdiq), with iqrar given precedence in outward legal rulings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you verbally declare your faith while your heart is far from conviction? What would it take today to align your inner tasdiq with your outer iqrar?
?
This lesson teaches that iqrar is first in manifestation, but tasdiq is the true beginning. Which one do you prioritize in your daily life—appearance before people or reality before Allah?
?
In your secret moments, are you one of the pious or one of the hypocrites that the Lawgiver does not differentiate from? What one concrete action can you take this week to strengthen your inner conviction so that your outer declaration is truthful?

Why Neither Iqrar nor Tasdiq Alone Suffices
Sanusi proves by Quranic evidence that both iqrar and tasdiq are required.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic proof that both iqrar and tasdiq are necessary for iman, using the examples of the hypocrites and the People of the Book.

Core Idea
Each component alone fails: hypocrites lack tasdiq, People of the Book lack proper iqrar.

Sanusi now quotes Imam al-A'zam to reinforce that neither iqrar alone nor tasdiq alone is sufficient. He provides two Quranic examples: the hypocrites who only declare verbally but are denounced as liars, and the People of the Book who know the truth inwardly but do not properly acknowledge the prophethood of Muhammad. This lesson shows why both elements are essential for true faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the quote from Imam al-A'zam
Read the Arabic and translation of the quote from 'Al-Wasiyya'. Notice how the Imam states the definition and then gives the hypothethical: if iqrar alone were iman, all hypocrites would be believers.
2
Examine the first Quranic proof: hypocrites
The author cites Quran 63:1, where Allah calls the hypocrites liars in their claim of faith because they lack tasdiq. This proves that iqrar without tasdiq is not iman.
The verse: 'And Allah bears witness that the hypocrites are certainly liars.'
3
Examine the second Quranic proof: People of the Book
The author cites Quran 2:146, where the People of the Book recognize Muhammad as they recognize their own sons, yet they are not believers because they did not properly acknowledge his universal prophethood.
Their knowledge (tasdiq) alone does not benefit them because their iqrar was incomplete.
4
Reflect on the implication
Understand that true iman requires both verbal declaration and heartfelt conviction. Neither can stand alone.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that merely declaring the shahada (iqrar) is sufficient for iman, even without inner conviction.
Correction: The passage proves that hypocrites who declared faith were condemned as liars, showing that iqrar without tasdiq is not true iman.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the People of the Book not become believers despite knowing the truth?
A) Because they did not have any inner conviction
B) Because they did not verbally acknowledge Muhammad's universal prophethood
C) Because they rejected all prophets
D) Because they were polytheists

Key Takeaway
Faith requires both verbal declaration and inner conviction; each alone is insufficient, as proven by the examples of hypocrites and People of the Book.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you pronounce the shahada with your tongue while your heart remains distant from its full meaning? How can you ensure your iqrar is backed by genuine tasdiq, not just habit?
?
The People of the Book knew the truth but failed to submit fully. Are there areas in your faith where you know the right path but hold back from complete surrender? What is one such area you will address today?
?
If your faith were tested like the hypocrites—where only your outward actions are visible—would your inner conviction match your words? What specific change would make your tasdiq as strong as your iqrar?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
7 min
The Distinct Roles of Tasdiq and Iqrar in Faith
Sanusi distinguishes between tasdiq as essential and iqrar as conditional, with the coercion exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that tasdiq is an essential pillar that never drops, while iqrar is a conditional pillar that can be excused under coercion, and the reasoning behind this distinction.

Core Idea
Inner conviction is indispensable; verbal declaration is conditional and drops under duress.

Sanusi now explains the precise theological roles of tasdiq and iqrar. Tasdiq is described as an 'essential pillar' (rukn hasan li'aynihi) that never falls away, while iqrar is a 'condition' or 'pillar for something else' (rukn hasan li-ghayrihi) that can be dropped under coercion. This distinction is supported by the natural role of the tongue as the interpreter of the heart and by Quranic evidence from Surah al-Nahl. The lesson concludes with a mention of scholarly differences on the exact nature of iqrar.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two categories of pillars
Read the description of tasdiq as a 'rukn hasan li'aynihi' and iqrar as a 'shart' or 'rukn hasan li-ghayrihi'. Grasp the difference: tasdiq is essential in itself; iqrar is conditional and can be excused.
The term 'hasan' here means complete or perfect in its category.
2
Learn the coercion exception
The author explains that if a person is coerced into denying faith verbally but maintains inner conviction, he does not become a disbeliever. The tongue's statement under duress does not reflect the heart.
Quran 16:106 is cited as evidence: 'except for one who is coerced while his heart is at rest with faith.'
3
Note the scholarly divergence
Some scholars, like al-Sarakhsi, consider iqrar as part of the essence of faith, while others like al-Nasafi and the Ash'aris consider it a condition for worldly rulings. Both views are mentioned.
This divergence does not affect the core position that tasdiq is always required.
4
Reflect on the wisdom
This shows that Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity; He judges the heart. The conditional nature of iqrar reflects mercy in times of duress.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإيمان هو الإقرار أي بلسانه بالتحقيق والتصديق أي بالجنان وفق التوفيق، وتقديم الإقرار للإشعار بأنه الأول في مقام الإظهار وإن كان الثاني هو المبدوء به في حال الاعتبار، ولأن الشارع اكتفى بمجرد الإقرار ولم يفرّق في الحكم بين المرافق والمنافق وبين الأبرار والفجار. وقال الإمام الأعظم في كتابه "الوصية": الإيمان إقرار باللسان وتصديق بالجنان، والإقرار وحده لا يكون إيمانا؛ لأنه لو كان إيمانا لكان المنافقون كلهم مؤمنين، وكذلك المعرفة وحدها أي مجرد التصديق لا يكون إيمانا؛ لأنها لو كانت إيمانا لكان أهل الكتاب كلهم مؤمنين، قال الله تعالى في حق المنافقين: وَاللهُ يَشْهَدُ إِنَّ الْمُنَافِقِينَ لَكَاذِبُونَ [المنافقون: ١]، أي في دعواهم الإيمان حيث لا تصديق لهم، وقال الله تعالى في حق أهل الكتاب: الَّذِينَ آتَيْنَاهُمُ الْكِتَابَ يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَهُمْ [البقرة: ١٤٦] انتهى. والمقصود أن مجرد معرفة أهل الكتاب بالله ورسوله لا ينفعهم حيث ما أقرّوا بنبوة محمد صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ورسالته إليهم وإلى الخلق كافة، فانهم كانوا يزعمون أنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم مبعوث إلى العرب خاصة، فإقرارهم بهذا الطريق لا يكون خالصاً. ثم التصديق ركن حسن لعينه لا يحتمل السقوط في حال من الأحوال بخلاف الإقرار، فإنه شرط أو شطر وركن حسن لغيره، ولهذا يسقط في حال الإكراه وحصول الأعذار. وهذا لأن اللسان ترجمان الجنان فيكون دليل التصديق وجوداً وعدماً، فإذا بدّله بغيره في وقت يكون متمكناً من إظهاره كان كافراً، وأما إذا زال تمكنه من الإظهار بالإكراه لم يصر كافراً؛ لأن سبب الخوف على نفسه دليل ظاهر على بقاء التصديق في قلبه وأن الحامل له على هذا التبديل حاجته إلى دفع المهلكة عن نفسه، لا تبديل الاعتقاد في حقه كما أشار إليه قوله تعالى: مَنْ كَفَرَ بِاللَّهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ إِيمَانِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنٌّ بِالْإِيمَانِ وَلَكِنْ مَنْ شَرَحَ بِالْكُفْرِ صَدْرًا فَعَلَيْهِمْ غَضَبٌ مِنَ اللَّهِ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ عَظِيمٌ [النحل: ١٠٦]، فأما تبديله في وقت تمكنه دليل على تبديل اعتقاده، فكان ركن الإيمان وجوداً وعدماً كما صرح به شمس الأئمة السرخسي، إلا أن صاحب "العُدة" وهو أبو البركات عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمود النسفي رحمه الله صرح بأن الإقرار شرط إجراء الأحكام وهو مختار الأشاعرة، وعليه أبو منصور الماتريدي، ثم في حذف المؤمن به في كلام الإمام الأعظم إشعار بأن الإيمان الإجمالي كاف في مقام المرام. فالتحقيق أن الإيمان هو تصديق النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم بالقلب في جميع ما علم بالضرورة مجيئه به من عند الله إجمالاً وأنه كاف في الخروج عن عهدة الإيمان ولا تنحط درجته عن الإيمان التفصيلي، كذا في "شرح العقائد"، إلا أن الأولى أن يقال: إجمالاً إن لوحظ
And faith (al-iman) is acknowledgement (al-iqrar) i.e. with the tongue, by verification, and inner conviction (al-tasdiq) i.e. with the heart, according to divine success. And the precedence of acknowledgement is to indicate that it is first in the position of manifestation, although inner conviction is the one that is started with in the case of consideration, and because the Lawgiver sufficed with mere acknowledgement and did not differentiate in the ruling between the pious and the hypocrite, nor between the righteous and the wicked. And Imam al-A'zam said in his book "Al-Wasiyya": Faith is acknowledgement with the tongue and inner conviction with the heart. Acknowledgement alone does not constitute faith; because if it were faith, all the hypocrites would be believers. Likewise, knowledge (al-ma'rifa) alone i.e. mere inner conviction does not constitute faith; because if it were faith, all the People of the Book would be believers. Allah Almighty said concerning the hypocrites: "And Allah bears witness that the hypocrites are certainly liars" [Qur'an 63:1], i.e. in their claim of faith while they have no inner conviction. And Allah Almighty said concerning the People of the Book: "Those whom We gave the Book recognize him as they recognize their own sons" [Qur'an 2:146]. End. And the meaning is that mere knowledge of the People of the Book about Allah and His Messenger does not benefit them since they did not acknowledge the prophethood of Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) and his message to them and to all creation, for they claimed that he (peace and blessings be upon him) was sent only to the Arabs specifically, so their acknowledgement in this way is not pure. Then inner conviction is an essential pillar in itself (rukn hasan li'aynihi) that cannot possibly fall away in any circumstance, unlike acknowledgement, for it is a condition (shart) or part (shatr) and a pillar for something else (rukn hasan li-ghayrihi). For this reason it falls away in the case of coercion and when excuses occur. This is because the tongue is the interpreter of the heart, so it is an indicator of inner conviction both in existence and absence. If one substitutes it with something else at a time when one is able to express it, he becomes a disbeliever. But if his ability to express it ceases due to coercion, he does not become a disbeliever, because the cause of fear for his life is an apparent indication of the persistence of inner conviction in his heart and that what drives him to this substitution is his need to repel harm from himself, not a change of belief in his case, as indicated by the saying of Allah Almighty: "Whoever disbelieves in Allah after his belief – except for one who is coerced while his heart is at rest with faith – but whoever opens their breast to disbelief, upon them is wrath from Allah and for them is a great punishment" [Qur'an 16:106]. As for his substituting it at a time when he is able, it is an indication of his belief change, so it becomes the pillar of faith both in existence and non-existence, as Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi stated. However, the author of "Al-'Umdah" – and he is Abu al-Barakat Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Mahmud al-Nasafi (may Allah have mercy on him) – stated that acknowledgement is a condition for the application of rulings, which is the choice of the Ash'aris, and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi also held this. Then, in the omission of the object of belief in the words of Imam al-A'zam, there is an indication that summary faith (al-iman al-ijmali) is sufficient in the intended purpose. The verification is that faith is inner conviction in the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) with the heart in all that is known by necessity to have come from him from Allah, summarily, and that it is sufficient to discharge the obligation of faith, and its rank is not lower than detailed faith (al-iman al-tafsili). Thus in "Sharh al-'Aqa'id", except that the better thing to say is: summarily if it is considered.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage defines faith (iman) and explains the roles of its two components: iqrar (verbal declaration) and tasdiq (inner conviction). The author begins by stating that iqrar is with the tongue and tasdiq with the heart, noting that iqrar is mentioned first to show it is the initial outward manifestation, though tasdiq is the starting point in consideration. The Lawgiver (the Prophet) accepted mere iqrar in rulings, not distinguishing between the pious and the hypocrite in outward judgment. The author then quotes Imam al-A'zam from his work 'Al-Wasiyya': iman is both iqrar and tasdiq; neither alone suffices. He supports this with Quranic evidence: the hypocrites are liars because they lack tasdiq, and the People of the Book know the truth but lack proper iqrar (they did not acknowledge Muhammad's prophet hood universally). The author then explains that tasdiq is an essential pillar that never falls away, while iqrar is a conditional pillar that drops under coercion. He elaborates: the tongue indicates what is in the heart; if one is able to express it but substitutes it, he becomes a disbeliever; if coerced, the fear shows tasdiq remains. He cites Quran 16:106. He then mentions scholarly views: Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi considered iqrar as an integral part of faith, while Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi and the Ash'aris considered it a condition for worldly rulings. He concludes that summary faith (tasdiq in all that the Prophet brought, without details) is sufficient and not inferior to detailed faith.

Key Terms
الركن (al-rukn)
الشرط (al-shart)
الشطر (al-shatr)
الإكراه (al-ikrah)
اللسان (al-lisan)
الترجمان (al-tarjuman)

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what happens to iqrar in cases of coercion?
A) It becomes even more important
B) It falls away and the person does not become a disbeliever
C) It is still required but with a lesser penalty
D) It is never excused under any circumstances

Key Takeaway
Inner conviction is always required; verbal declaration is conditional and can be forfeited under coercion, reflecting the principle that Allah judges the heart.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you allowed fear of people's opinions to shape your outward expressions of faith, even while your inner conviction remained? What does this lesson reveal about the state of your heart in those moments?
?
If you were faced with a situation where denying your faith verbally would save your life, would your heart be at rest with faith like the coerced believer in the verse? How can you strengthen your tasdiq today so that it remains unshakable?
?
This lesson teaches that voluntary substitution of iqrar indicates a change of belief. Search your own life: are there areas where you have willingly downplayed or hidden your faith for worldly gain? What does that say about the sincerity of your conviction?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
4 min
Summary Faith is Sufficient
Sanusi explains that summary faith (ijmali) is sufficient and not inferior to detailed faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that summary faith (al-iman al-ijmali) – believing in all that the Prophet brought, without detailed knowledge – is sufficient for true iman and not inferior to detailed faith (al-iman al-tafsili).

Core Idea
Believing in general everything the Prophet brought suffices for faith.

Sanusi concludes the discussion by addressing the sufficiency of summary faith. He notes that Imam al-A'zam omitted the object of belief ('in all that he brought') in his definition, which indicates that a general, summarized belief is enough. He then cites the view from 'Sharh al-Aqa'id' that summary faith is not lower in rank than detailed faith. This lesson clarifies that one does not need to know every detail of religion to be a believer; the essence is affirming the message as a whole.

Guided Path
1
Examine the omission in the Imam's definition
Sanusi points out that Imam al-A'zam did not explicitly mention 'in all that Muhammad brought' in his definition, hinting that a summarized belief is sufficient.
2
Understand what summary faith means
Summary faith is to believe in the Prophet's message overall, without specifying each particular. It is valid and sufficient to discharge the obligation of faith.
This is the position of the Maturidi school.
3
Compare summary and detailed faith
The text notes that summary faith is not of a lower rank than detailed faith; both are valid. Detailed faith is commendable but not obligatory.
4
Reflect on the implication
This teaching ensures that ordinary believers who cannot study all details are not disadvantaged. Faith is accessible to all.

He supports this with Quranic evidence: the hypocrites are liars because they lack tasdiq, and the People of the Book know the truth but lack proper iqrar (they did not acknowledge Muhammad's prophet hood universally). The author then explains that tasdiq is an essential pillar that never falls away, while iqrar is a conditional pillar that drops under coercion. He elaborates: the tongue indicates what is in the heart; if one is able to express it but substitutes it, he becomes a disbeliever; if coerced, the fear shows tasdiq remains. He cites Quran 16:106. He then mentions scholarly views: Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi considered iqrar as an integral part of faith, while Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi and the Ash'aris considered it a condition for worldly rulings. He concludes that summary faith (tasdiq in all that the Prophet brought, without details) is sufficient and not inferior to detailed faith.

Key Terms
الإيمان الإجمالي (al-iman al-ijmali)
الإيمان التفصيلي (al-iman al-tafsili)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the omission of the object of belief in Imam al-A'zam's definition indicate, according to Sanusi?
A) That detailed faith is required
B) That summary faith is sufficient
C) That faith can be without any knowledge
D) That only the tongue is needed

Key Takeaway
Summary faith – believing in the Prophet's message as a whole – is sufficient for true iman and is not of a lower rank than detailed faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever secretly feel that your faith is incomplete or that you are a lesser believer because you haven't mastered every detail of Islamic theology? How does this lesson challenge that insecurity, and will you actually let go of that burden today?
?
If you have more detailed knowledge than someone else, do you look down on them or consider their iman insufficient? What would it take for you to genuinely believe that their summary faith is fully acceptable before Allah?
?
This lesson says summary faith is enough. But does your heart truly rest in that, or do you still feel the need to 'prove' your faith through exhaustive study? What would change in your daily life if you fully trusted that your general belief in the Prophet suffices?

Iqrar: Condition for Worldly Rulings, Not Essence of Faith
The author contrasts two scholarly views on iqrar and presents the majority position with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the majority of verifiers (jumhur al-muhaqqiqin) treat iqrar as a condition for worldly rulings rather than part of the essence of iman.

Core Idea
Faith is in the heart; iqrar is only the outward sign for worldly dealings.

The precise definition of iman has been a key debate in Islamic theology. This passage presents the position of the majority of authoritative scholars (al-muhaqqiqin) that iman is fundamentally inner affirmation (tasdiq bi'l-qalb). Verbal confession (iqrar) is a separate requirement—necessary for applying Islamic legal rulings in this world, but not part of the reality of faith itself. This view, championed by Imam al-Maturidi, is supported by clear scriptural evidence grounding faith in the heart.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The passage first mentions a view that iqrar is a pillar (rukn), then presents the majority view. Note how each is framed.
The minority view allows iqrar to be dropped under coercion.
2
Understand the role of iqrar
According to the majority, iqrar is a condition (shart) for worldly rulings, not a pillar. Why? Because inner belief is hidden and needs a sign.
3
Examine the scriptural proofs
The passage cites Quranic verses (e.g., 58:22, 16:106, 49:14) and a hadith about Usama to show that faith is located in the heart.
These texts emphasize inner conviction over verbal declaration.
4
Apply the distinction
Consider the cases: a believer who cannot confess, and a hypocrite who confesses without belief. How does the majority view handle them?
The former is a believer before Allah but not in worldly rulings; the latter is opposite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعتبار الإقرار في مفهوم الإيمان مذهب بعض العلماء، وهو اختيار الإمام شمس الأئمة الحلواني وفخر الإسلام من أن الإقرار ركن إلا أنه قد يحتمل السقوط كما في حالة الإكراه، وذهب جمهور المحققين إلى أن الإيمان هو التصديق بالقلب. وإنما الإقرار شرط لإجراء الأحكام في الدنيا لما أن تصديق القلب أمر باطني لابد له من علامة، فمن صدق بقلبه ولم يقر بلسانه فهو مؤمن عند الله تعالى، وإن لم يكن مؤمنا في أحكام الدنيا، ومن أقر بلسانه ولم يصدق بقلبه كالمنافق فهو بالعكس، وهذا هو اختيار الشيخ أبي منصور الماتريدي رحمه الله والنصوص موافقة لذلك كقوله تعالى: ﴿أُولَئِكَ كَتَبَ فِي قُلُوبِهِمُ الْإِيمَانَ﴾ [المجادلة: 22]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنٌّ بِالْإِيمَانِ﴾ [النحل: 106]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَمَّا يَدْخُلِ الْإِيمَانُ فِي قُلُوبِكُمْ﴾ [الحجرات: 14]، وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لأسامة حين قتل من قال لا إله إلا الله: هلا شققت قلبه فنظرت أصادق هو أم كاذب؟
Then considering iqrar (verbal confession) in the concept of faith (iman) is the school of some scholars, and it is the choice of Imam Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani and Fakhr al-Islam that iqrar is a pillar, except that it may be dropped, as in the case of coercion. And the majority of the verifiers (jumhur al-muhaqqiqin) held that faith is affirmation with the heart (tasdiq bi'l-qalb), and iqrar is only a condition for the execution of [worldly] rulings in this world, because affirmation of the heart is an inward matter that must have a sign. Thus, whoever affirms with his heart but does not confess with his tongue is a believer in the sight of Allah the Exalted, even if he is not a believer in the rulings of this world. And whoever confesses with his tongue but does not affirm with his heart, like the hypocrite, it is the opposite. This is the choice of Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (may Allah have mercy on him), and the texts agree with that, such as His statement the Exalted: 'Those are the ones in whose hearts He has inscribed faith' [Surah al-Mujadilah: 22], and His statement the Exalted: 'And his heart is at rest with faith' [Surah al-Nahl: 106], and His statement the Exalted: 'And faith has not yet entered into your hearts' [Surah al-Hujurat: 14], and his statement (peace and blessings be upon him) to Usama when he killed the one who said 'There is no god but Allah': 'Why did you not split open his heart and see whether he is truthful or a liar?'
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage presents the differing views on whether iqrar (verbal confession) is part of the definition of iman. The author first mentions the position of some scholars, including Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani and Fakhr al-Islam, who consider iqrar to be a pillar (rukn) of iman, but with the exception that it can be dropped in cases of coercion (ikrah). This view aligns with the earlier opinion of al-Sarakhsi. The author then presents the preferred view of the majority of verifiers (jumhur al-muhaqqiqin): iman is exclusively tasdiq bi'l-qalb (affirmation with the heart). Iqrar is not part of the essence of iman; rather, it is a condition (shart) for applying Islamic rulings in this world (ijra' al-ahkam). The reason is that inner belief is hidden and requires an external sign for worldly purposes. Therefore, a person who truly believes in his heart but does not verbalize is a believer in the sight of Allah, though not considered a believer in Islamic legal rulings (e.g., inheritance, marriage). Conversely, a hypocrite who verbally confesses but does not believe is not a believer before Allah, even though he is treated as a Muslim in worldly matters. The author identifies this as the view of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and supports it with scriptural evidence: Qur'anic verses that locate iman in the heart (e.g., 'inscribed faith in their hearts', 'his heart is at rest with faith', 'faith has not entered your hearts') and the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) rebuked Usama for killing a man who said the shahada, telling him to check the man's heart. This reinforces the primacy of inner conviction over verbal declaration.

مذهب بعض العلماء
جمهور المحققين
التصديق بالقلب
شرط إجراء الأحكام
المنافق
أبو منصور الماتريدي
شمس الأئمة الحلواني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That iqrar is always part of iman and necessary for one's status before Allah.
Correction: The majority view holds that iqrar is only a condition for worldly rulings; inner faith alone suffices before Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the majority of verifiers (jumhur al-muhaqqiqin), what is the status of a person who affirms faith in his heart but never verbally confesses?
A) He is a believer both before Allah and in worldly rulings.
B) He is a believer before Allah but not in worldly rulings.
C) He is not a believer in any sense because he did not confess.
D) He is a hypocrite because he hid his faith.

Key Takeaway
The majority view holds that iman is inner affirmation; iqrar is only necessary for worldly legal rulings, not for the reality of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the shahada, is your heart genuinely at rest with faith, or are you merely going through the motions? What concrete signs in your daily life reveal the state of your inner iman?
?
If you were in a situation where professing Islam could lead to severe persecution, would your inner affirmation be strong enough to sustain you as a believer in Allah's sight even if you remained silent? Where is your true security—in the approval of people or in the knowledge of Allah?

The hypocrite utters the words but the heart is empty. Have you ever caught yourself saying 'Alhamdulillah' or 'Jazakallah' without feeling their weight? What is one step you will take today to ensure your tongue and heart are aligned?

The Essence of Iman: Fixed Tasdiq, Varying Certainty
The author refutes the Karamiyya definition of Iman and explains its true nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the essence of iman is heart affirmation (tasdiq), which does not increase or decrease, but the level of certainty (yaqin) can vary, and that this refutes the Karamiyya claim that iman is merely verbal declaration.

Core Idea
Iman is one in essence but varies in certainty.

Sanusi begins by establishing the true nature of iman against the Karamiyya sect. He shows that iman is tasdiq in the heart, not just words, and that while the object of faith is fixed, the strength of conviction differs. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its implications for understanding faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the consensus statement
Read the opening sentence that establishes consensus on the iman of a person unable to declare verbally. Notice how this already refutes the Karamiyya position.
The consensus includes those prevented by muteness or similar.
2
Identify the refutation of Karamiyya
Find the sentence where the author explicitly rejects the Karamiyya definition of iman as mere shahada. Understand that tasdiq (heart affirmation) is essential.
The refutation is direct and uses the consensus as evidence.
3
Understand the no-increase/no-decrease principle
The author states that iman does not increase or decrease with respect to the object of faith itself. Focus on the phrase 'min haythu asl al-tasdiq' – the essence of affirmation is the same for all believers.
This does not mean all believers are equal in certainty or deeds.
4
Explore the Abraham verse and levels of yaqin
Read the Quranic verse about Ibrahim asking for reassurance. The author uses it to show that 'ayn al-yaqin is higher than 'ilm al-yaqin, proving that certainty varies even though the core iman is one.
This is a key example of varying certainty within the same iman.
5
Connect to learning objective
Summarize how the passage teaches that iman's essence is fixed (tasdiq) while its strength (yaqin) admits degrees. Reflect on why this matters for theology.
This refutes both the Karamiyya and those who claim iman increases with deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإجماع منعقد على إيمان من صدق بقلبه وقصد الإقرار بلسانه ومنعه مانع من خرس ونحوه. فظهر أن حقيقة الإيمان ليست مجرد كلمتي الشهادة على ما زعمت الكرامية. وإيمان أهل السماء أي من الملائكة وأهل الجنة والأرض أي من الأنبياء والأولياء وسائر المؤمنين من الأبرار والفجار لا يزيد ولا ينقص أي من جهة المؤمن به نفسه؛ لأن التصديق إذا لم يكن على وجه التحقيق يكون في مرتبة الظن والترديد، والظن غير مفيد في مقام الاعتقاد عند أرباب التأييد، قال الله تعالى: {إِنَّ الظَّنَّ لا يُغْنِى مِنَ الْحَقِّ شَيًا} [يونس: 36]. فالتحقيق أن الإيمان كما قال الإمام الرازي لا يقبل الزيادة والنقصان من حيثية أصل التصديق لا من جهة اليقين فإن مراتب أهلها مختلفة في كمال الدين كما أشار إليه سبحانه بقوله: {وَإِذْ قَالَ إِبْرَاهِمُ رَبِّ أَرِنِي كَيْفَ تُحْيِي الْمَوْتَى قَالَ أَوَلَمْ تُؤْمِن قَالَ بَلَى وَلَكِن لِّيَطْمَئِنَّ قَلْبِي} [البقرة: 260] فإن مرتبة عين اليقين فوق مرتبة علم اليقين.
Consensus is affirmed upon the faith of one who affirms [truth] with his heart and intends to declare with his tongue but is prevented by a hindrance such as muteness or the like. Thus it becomes clear that the reality of faith is not merely the two words of shahada as the Karamiyya claimed. And the faith of the inhabitants of heaven, i.e., the angels and the people of Paradise, and earth, i.e., the prophets, saints, and all the believers, both righteous and wicked, does not increase or decrease, i.e., with respect to the object of faith itself; because affirmation (tasdiq) if it is not in the manner of certainty (tahqiq) is in the rank of doubt and hesitation, and doubt is of no use in the station of belief according to the people of confirmation. Allah the Exalted said: 'Indeed, assumption does not avail against the truth at all' [Yunus: 36]. So the verification is that faith, as Imam al-Razi said, does not admit of increase or decrease with respect to the principle of affirmation (asl al-tasdiq), but not with respect to certainty (yaqin), for its ranks among its people differ in the perfection of religion, as the Exalted alluded to with His saying: 'And [mention] when Abraham said, 'My Lord, show me how You give life to the dead.' [Allah] said, 'Have you not believed?' He said, 'Yes, but [I ask] that my heart may be satisfied.' [Al-Baqarah: 260]. For the rank of the eye of certainty ('ayn al-yaqin) is above the rank of the knowledge of certainty ('ilm al-yaqin).
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage defines the nature of true Iman and refutes the Karamiyya claim. It begins by stating that there is consensus (ijma) that a person who believes in his heart and intends to utter the shahada but is prevented by a legitimate excuse (like muteness) is still considered a believer. This refutes the Karamiyya who say Iman is merely uttering the two shahada statements. Then it explains that the Iman of all believers—angels, prophets, saints, and ordinary believers—does not increase or decrease in its essence, i.e., the object of belief itself is the same. However, because tasdiq (affirmation) can be at different levels of certainty, doubt is not sufficient for true belief. The author quotes the Quranic verse that assumption (zann) does not avail against truth. He then cites Imam al-Razi's position: Iman does not increase or decrease in its principle (asl al-tasdiq), but it differs in terms of yaqin (certainty). He gives the example of Prophet Ibrahim (AS) who had Iman but asked for a higher level of certainty (itmi'nan), showing that 'ayn al-yaqin is above 'ilm al-yaqin. This passage thus establishes that the core of Iman is tasdiq, which is fixed, but the strength of conviction can vary.

Key Terms
إيمان (Iman)
تصديق (Tasdiq)
يقين (Yaqin)
كرامية (Karamiyya)
عين اليقين ('Ayn al-Yaqin)
علم اليقين ('Ilm al-Yaqin)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Iman is merely verbal declaration.
Correction: Iman is primarily heart affirmation (tasdiq); verbal declaration is a necessary outward expression but not the essence.

Checkpoint
What is the main point the author makes about the essence of Iman?
A) It increases with good deeds and decreases with sins
B) It is merely uttering the shahada
C) It does not increase or decrease in its essence, but certainty varies
D) It is the same for all believers without any difference

Key Takeaway
The essence of iman is fixed tasdiq, but certainty (yaqin) admits degrees, as shown by the example of Prophet Ibrahim.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Prophet Ibrahim, already a prophet, asked for a sign to increase his heart's satisfaction. What sign do you need from Allah today to move your Iman from mere knowledge to a certainty that transforms your life? And what prevents you from asking for it?
?
The passage warns that doubt (zann) is of no use in belief. In what area of your faith do you allow assumptions or hesitations to linger—about Allah's attributes, His promise, or His decree? How long will you let that doubt steal the strength of your Iman?

Increase and Decrease of Iman: Strength and Weakness
The author explains that increase and decrease of Iman refer to strength and weakness of certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the increase and decrease of Iman (faith) refer to the strength and weakness of certainty, not a change in its essence.

Core Idea
Iman increases and decreases in strength, not in essence.

This lesson clarifies a key theological point about Iman. The author addresses a hadith about seeing vs. news and explains that increase and decrease in Iman mean the strengthening or weakening of certainty, not a change in the fundamental belief. This resolves a verbal dispute among scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the opening hadith and the objection about certainty.
The passage uses the example of knowing the Kaaba from a distance vs. seeing it directly.
2
Understand the Meaning of Increase
The author clarifies that increase and decrease refer to strength and weakness of certainty, not to an essential change. See the analogy of affirming the sunrise vs. affirming the world's creation.
Both affirmations are equally belief (tasdiq), but one is stronger.
3
Recognize the Verbal Dispute
The author concludes that the disagreement about whether Iman increases is verbal (lafzi) among the people of gnosis, because they all agree on the underlying reality.
The hadith about Abu Bakr's faith outweighing others is interpreted as relating to strength of certainty, not external deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا ورد: «ليس الخبر كالمعاينة وإن قال بعضهم: لو كشف الغطاء ما ازددت يقينا»، أصلا اليقين لمطابقة العلم اليقين في ذلك الحين، وهو لا ينافي زيادة اليقين عند الرؤية، كما هو مشاهد لمن له علم بالكعبة في الغيبة ثم حصل له المشاهدة في عالم الحضرة، وعلى هذا فالمراد بالزيادة والنقصان القوة والضعف، فإن التصديق بطلوع الشمس أقوى من التصديق بحدوث العالم، وإن كانا متساويين في أصل تصديق المؤمن به، ونحن نعلم قطعا أن إيمان آحاد الأمة ليس كإيمان النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ولا كإيمان أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه باعتبار هذا التحقيق، وهذا معنى ما ورد: «لو وزن إيمان أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه بإيمان جميع المؤمنين لرجح إيمانه». يعني لرجحان إيقانه ووقار جنانه وثبات إتقانه وتحقيق عرفانه، لا من جهة ثمرات الإيمان من زيادات الإحسان لتفاوت أفراد الإنسان من أهل الإيمان في كثرة الطاعات وقلة العصيان وعكسه في مرتبة النقصان مع بقاء أصل وصف الإيمان في حق كل منهما بنعت الإيقان، فالخلاف لفظي بين أرباب العرفان.
Similarly, it is reported: 'News is not like direct observation, though some say: If the veil were lifted, I would not increase in certainty' – the principle of certainty is that the knowledge of certainty ('ilm al-yaqin) matches it at that time, and this does not negate the increase of certainty at the time of seeing, as is witnessed by one who has knowledge of the Kaaba while absent and then obtains direct vision in the state of presence. Based on this, what is meant by increase and decrease is strength and weakness. For the affirmation of the rising of the sun is stronger than the affirmation of the occurrence of the world, even though they are equal in the principle of affirmation (asl al-tasdiq) of the believer. And we know definitively that the faith of the common people of the ummah is not like the faith of the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) nor like the faith of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) by this verification. This is the meaning of what has been reported: 'If the faith of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq were weighed against the faith of all the believers, his faith would outweigh.' i.e., due to the preponderance of his certainty, the dignity of his heart, the firmness of his mastery, and the realization of his gnosis, not due to the fruits of faith from increases in excellence, due to the variation of individuals among the people of faith in abundance of acts of obedience and paucity of disobedience and its opposite in the degree of deficiency, while the original description of faith remains in each of them with the attribute of certainty. Thus the disagreement is verbal among the people of gnosis.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage explains the meaning of increase and decrease in Iman. It begins by citing a hadith: 'News is not like seeing,' and addresses an objection that some might claim they wouldn't increase in certainty even if the veil were lifted. The author clarifies that this statement refers to the inherent certainty matching 'ilm al-yaqin, but does not negate an increase of certainty upon direct vision (like seeing the Kaaba after only knowing about it). Therefore, the increase and decrease in Iman refer to strength and weakness (quwwa wa du'f). He gives the example that affirming the sun's rising is stronger than affirming the occurrence of the world, although both are equally affirmed in principle. Then he states that we know definitively that the Iman of ordinary believers is not like that of the Prophet or Abu Bakr. He interprets the hadith about weighing Abu Bakr's Iman as referring to the strength of his certainty and inner qualities, not to external acts of obedience. Thus, the disagreement about whether Iman increases or decreases is verbal (lafzi) according to the people of gnosis ('urafan).

Key Terms
زيادة (Ziyada)
نقصان (Nuqsan)
قوة (Quwwa)
ضعف (Du'f)
يقين (Yaqin)
مشاهدة (Mushahada)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the increase in Iman refers to adding something to the essence of belief.
Correction: The increase and decrease refer to the strength and weakness of certainty, not a change in the essence of Iman.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does 'increase and decrease' in Iman mean?
A) The number of beliefs held
B) The strength and weakness of certainty
C) The amount of knowledge about Allah
D) The performance of good deeds

Key Takeaway
The increase and decrease of Iman refer to the strength and weakness of certainty, not a change in its essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you compare your own faith to that of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, are you more discouraged or inspired? What would it mean for you to focus on the strength of your certainty rather than measuring your deeds against his?
?
The author says the disagreement about increase and decrease is only verbal among the people of gnosis. Are you more concerned with the state of your heart before Allah or with winning theological arguments? How would your life change if you prioritized strengthening your yaqin over debating its definition?
?
If you had the chance to see the Kaaba directly after only knowing about it, would you expect your certainty to increase? What does your answer reveal about the connection between direct experience and faith? Are you actively seeking means to strengthen your certainty, or are you satisfied with secondhand knowledge?

Imam Muhammad's Prohibition on Saying 'My Iman is Like Jibreel's'
Imam Muhammad's ruling on a specific expression about faith and Jibreel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Muhammad prohibited a specific expression about one's faith in relation to the angel Jibreel, and what expression he recommended instead.

Core Idea
Words matter in faith: claiming equality with Jibreel's Iman can mislead.

Imam Muhammad, a prominent student of Imam Abu Hanifa, addressed a seemingly subtle issue of phrasing when expressing one's faith. He cautioned against saying 'my Iman is like the Iman of Jibreel' because it might imply a level of perfection that is not true for human beings. Instead, he prescribed a more precise formulation. Let's read his ruling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the two expressions: the disliked one and the recommended one.
The passage is a quote from al-Khulasa.
2
Understand the reasoning
The passage explains why the first expression is disliked: it may suggest equality in all respects. Reflect on why this is problematic.
3
Apply the lesson
Consider how careful wording in matters of faith prevents misunderstandings.
This is a practical example of theological precision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن هنا قال الإمام محمد رحمه الله على ما ذكره في "الخلاصة" عنه: «أكره أن يقول إيماني كإيمان جبرائيل عليه السلام ولكن يقول آمنت بما آمن به جبرائيل عليه السلام»، انتهى. وذلك أن إيمانه كإيمان جبرائيل عليه السلام من جميع الوجوه، وليس الأمر كذلك لما أن الأول يوهم هو الفرق البين بينهما هنالك. قال الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله في كتابه "الوصية": ثم الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص، لأنه لا يتصور زيادة الإيمان إلا بنقصان الكفر، ولا يتصور نقصان الإيمان إلا بزيادة الكفر، فكيف يجوز؟
And from here, Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said, as mentioned in 'al-Khulasa' from him: 'I dislike that one should say 'My faith is like the faith of Jibril (peace be upon him)', but rather let him say 'I believe in what Jibril (peace be upon him) believed in'.' End. This is because his [Jibril's] faith is like the faith of Jibril (peace be upon him) in all respects, and it is not so because the first expression might suggest the obvious difference between them there. Imam al-A'zam (may Allah have mercy on him) said in his book 'al-Wasiyya': 'Then faith does not increase nor decrease, because an increase in faith cannot be imagined except by a decrease in disbelief, and a decrease in faith cannot be imagined except by an increase in disbelief. So how could that be permissible?'
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage contains two separate proofs. First, Imam Muhammad (Abu Hanifa's student) dislikes a person saying 'My Iman is like the Iman of Jibreel', because that might imply equality in all respects, whereas there is a clear difference in the strength of certainty. Instead, one should say 'I believe in what Jibreel believed in,' which affirms the same object of belief without claiming equal certainty. Second, Imam Abu Hanifa in his 'al-Wasiyya' gives a logical argument: Faith cannot increase or decrease because increase in Iman would require a decrease in kufr (disbelief), and decrease in Iman would require increase in kufr. Since Iman and kufr are opposites, they cannot coexist in the same person in that sense. Thus, Iman's essence is fixed. This reinforces the earlier discussion that any variation is in strength, not in reality.

جبرائيل
أكره

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Saying 'my Iman is like the Iman of Jibreel' is permissible without issue.
Correction: Imam Muhammad explicitly dislikes it because it implies equality in all respects, which is false.

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Muhammad dislike saying 'My Iman is like the Iman of Jibreel'?
A) Because Jibreel is an angel and not human
B) Because it might imply equality in all respects when there is a clear difference
C) Because Jibreel's Iman is unknown
D) Because it is disrespectful to Jibreel

Key Takeaway
Imam Muhammad teaches us to avoid expressions that could imply false equality in faith, and instead to affirm belief in the same truths.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'my Iman is like...' what does that reveal about your tendency to measure faith by comparison rather than by its content? How can you train yourself to affirm what you believe without comparing it to others' faith?
?
What other phrases do you use in daily speech about your faith that might imply something inaccurate? Identify one and, based on this lesson, rephrase it to avoid false implications.
?
Think of a time you compared your Iman to someone else's—whether feeling superior or inferior. What did that comparison say about your focus? This week, will you commit to simply focusing on believing in what the angels believe in, without comparison?

Imam Abu Hanifa's Argument: Faith Does Not Increase or Decrease
Imam Abu Hanifa's logical proof of the immutability of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Abu Hanifa's logical argument for why faith (Iman) cannot increase or decrease in its essence.

Core Idea
Faith cannot increase because that would require disbelief to decrease, which is impossible.

Imam Abu Hanifa presents a concise logical proof that faith is immutable in its reality. He argues that increase in faith would necessitate a decrease in disbelief, and vice versa, but since the two cannot coexist as opposites in the same person, faith's essence must be fixed. Let's see how he reasons.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the source passage and translation. Notice the two conditional statements.
2
Understand the logic
The argument uses the principle of opposites: increase in Iman implies decrease in Kufr, and decrease in Iman implies increase in Kufr. Since Iman and Kufr are opposites, such exchange would change the person's state radically. Therefore, Iman does not admit increase/decrease in its essence.
3
Connect to earlier lessons
This reinforces that variations in faith refer only to degrees of certainty, not to its fundamental nature.

?
